About the Fraser Valley
                                                                  The FVRD receives its authority to govern through the Letters
                                                                  Patent, Service Area Establishment bylaws and under the

Regional District (FVRD)

                                                                  Columbia. Regional District bylaws for services must be                 SQUAMISH-LILOOET RD                                                                                 THOMPSON-NICOLA RD

            to develop situational awareness and formulate objectives
            during each of the four phases of emergency management.

                        Emergency Management
                                                                                      Section 3 of the recently adopted, modernized Emergency
                                                                                      and Disaster Management Act describes the four phases as

                        Structure and Service
                                                                                      follows:



                                                                                      01 MITIGATION
EMERGENCY                                                                             The mitigation phase, in which measures are taken for the
                                                                                      purposes of identifying and removing or reducing hazards
MANAGEMENT                                                                            so as to:


STRUCTURE AND SERVICE
                                                                                      »   Prevent emergencies from occurring, or
                        FOUR PHASES OF EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT                           »   Reduce, to the extent reasonably practicable, the
                        Emergency and disaster management in BC takes an “all             scale, scope, and adverse effects of an emergency
                        hazards” approach.                                                that may occur


                            Emergency management adopts an all-hazards
                            approach in every jurisdiction in Canada by addressing    02 PREPARATION
                            vulnerabilities exposed by both natural and human-        The preparation phase, in which measures are taken for
                            induced hazards and disasters. The all-hazards approach   the purpose of establishing the knowledge, capability, and
                            increases efficiency by recognizing and integrating       capacity to anticipate, respond to, and recover from the
                            common emergency management elements across all           adverse effects of an emergency
                            hazard types, and then supplementing these common

                                                                                      03 RESPONSE
                            elements with hazard-specific sub-components to
                            fill gaps only as required. As such, “all hazards” does
                            not literally mean preparing to address any and all
                            potential hazards in existence. Rather, it emphasizes     The response phase, in which measures are taken for
                            the leveraging of synergies common across hazards         the purpose of responding to an emergency, including
                            and maintaining a streamlined and robust emergency        preventing and reducing the adverse effects of the
                            management system. The all hazards approach also          emergency
                            improves the ability of emergency management

                                                                                      04 RECOVERY
                            activities to address unknown hazards or risks. (An
                            Emergency Management Framework for Canada, Third
                            Edition, 2017)
                                                                                      The recovery phase, in which measures are taken for the
                                                                                      purpose of recovering from an emergency, including
                        This all hazards emergency management approach is             measures to:
                        divided into four phases. These phases may be referred to
                                                                                      »   Restore the health, safety and well-being of affected
                        as the “four pillars of emergency management”, the “four
                                                                                          persons
                        phases of the emergency management cycle”, or the “four
                        phases of the emergency management continuum”. In all         »   Restore the safety of property or of objects or sites of
                        cases, the four phases being referred to are:                     heritage value
                                                                                      »   Improve, to the extent reasonably practicable, assets,
                        »   01 Mitigation                                                 services, and processes so as to reduce the risk of
                        »   02 Preparation                                                and increase resilience to emergencies

                        »   03 Response
                        »   04 Recovery

                                                                                                                                                                                During the creation of this EMP, the Province of British
                                                                                                                  PROVINCIAL EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT
                                                                                                                                                                                Columbia adopted a new Emergency and Disaster
                                                                                                                  STRUCTURE                                                     Management Act, which replaces the Emergency Program
                                                                                                                  Emergency management authorities, legislation, and            Act. The updated legislation shifts to focusing on emergency
                                                                                                                  statutory obligations are currently laid out by the           response across all four phases of emergency management.
                                                                                                                  Province of British Columbia in the Emergency and Disaster    As part of the phased implementation of the proposed



                                                        04
                                                                                                                  Management Act 2023, the BC Emergency Program                 legislation, the Province of British Columbia is developing
                                                                                                                                                                                various regulations that are anticipated to be introduced
                                    RECOVERY
                                                                                                                  Management Regulation, the BC Compensation and
                                                                                                                  Disaster Financial Assistance Regulation, and the BC Local    starting in late 2023 and through 2025.
                                                                                                                  Authority Emergency Management Regulation.
                                                                                                                                                                                Until those legislative and regulatory updates are adopted
                                                                                                                  Modernized emergency management legislation has been          and implemented, the FVRD must continue to follow
                                                                                                                  developed by the Province of British Columbia that will       the existing legislation and regulations. The Ministry of
                                                                                                                  address new standards and best practices garnered from:       Emergency Management and Climate Readiness (EMCR)
                                                                                                                                                                                is BC’s lead coordinating agency for all emergency
                                                                              MITIGATION                                                                                        management activities, including preparations, response,

                                                                                                                  »   The Sendai Framework for Disaster Risk Reduction
                                                                                                                                                                                recovery, and mitigation. They are responsible for managing

                                                                                                                                                                             FVRD emergency management regulations are established in its bylaw cited
                                                                                                                                                                             as, “Fraser Valley Regional District Emergency Management Regulations Bylaw
                                                                                  CAO                                         Board Chair                                    No.1622, 2021”. This bylaw applies equilaterally to all eight unincorporated
                                                                                                                                                                             areas under the FVRD’s jurisdiction. It establishes an Emergency Management
                                                                                                                                                                             Organization (EMO) to provide strategic oversight of the EM Program. The EMO
                                                         EMERGENCY OPERATIONS CENTRE DIRECTOR                                 Provincial Regional
                                                                                                                                                                             consists of the FVRD Board, the Emergency Management Executive Committee,
                                                                                                                              Coordination Level
                                                                                                                                                                             the Director of Emergency Management (DEM), and the EM staff. The EMO
                                                                                                                              (PREOC)
                                                                                                  Risk management                                                            oversees the development and implementation of the EM Program, policies, and
                                                                                                                                                                             plans associated with mitigation, preparation, response, and recovery measures
                                                                                                                                                                             within the FVRD electoral areas.
                                                Deputy Director                                   Liaison                     Agency representatives

                                                                                                       Public information                                                                                          ensuring sufficient budget and resources; and appointing the DEM.

FVRD EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT SERVICE
Within the FVRD, it is critical to understand that beyond
the EMO, the entire FVRD organization is engaged in
providing emergency management service across all four                                         OTHER
                                                                                                                                              PART 3
phases of emergency management. The EMO develops                                                                   FVRD
and maintains the EM Program. The EM Program identifies
critical program activities and priorities in each of the four
                                                                              RAIL &                                                          FVRD EMERGENCY
                                                                            TRANSPORT
phases and integrates all of the FVRD functions, all five
FVRD departments, personnel, volunteers, infrastructure,
                                                                                                                                EMCR          MANAGEMENT
and facilities in order to achieve them.
                                                                                                 OUR SHARED                                   PROGRAM
Zooming out from the FVRD as an organization to the                         FORTIS              RESPONSIBILITY
FVRD as a regional geography, there are many entities with                                                                       BC
responsibilities, jurisdictional authority, and/or capacity to                                                                WILDFIRE
support services. Residents also have an important role to
play in each of the four emergency management phases.
Emergency management is a shared responsibility, and                                 TELUS
                                                                                                                      MOTI
government and non-government sectors must work                                                       BC
together. Engagement, collaboration, and coordination
are essential to maximizing the effectiveness of the                                                HYDRO
service.

In general, the FVRD has an Indigenous Relations Program,          »   Flood response guidance
the vision of which includes First Nations shaping the future
of the FVRD by sharing with it knowledge, resources, and
culture as respectful partners in planning. This vision is         Operational Readiness
guided by the following core values:
                                                                   »   Maintaining an EOC location

Specifically, the FVRD EM Program aspires to incorporate
cultural safety, intersectionality, reconciliation, and cultural   »   Supporting personal preparedness
resources in every aspect of its service delivery. The EM
                                                                   »   Building community capacity
Program is provided to the EM Service Participating Area—
the electoral areas off reserve, and does not include member
municipalities or First Nations communities. However,
collaboration and cross-jurisdictional coordination with
the 30 First Nations that manage 146 reserves that are
geographically co-located within the electoral areas
is key. Opportunities include integrated planning and
engagement, and, whenever possible, the FVRD invites
participation in training and exercise sessions and aims to
be an allied partner in collaborative capacity development.
